<ul><li>How fast would this be? I don&#39;t need the queries to be sub-second, but not taking 5min would be nice. </li><li>What other components do I need? <div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1319648345484034130 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1319648345484034130><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/984386111709253672/23fac11e09942718016d6d4c58935a2e.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/870635915461156917/081e4c67ed8dfab5a18e68b34715fa0d.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=aarthex>Arthex</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1319431291300483154')"> So, a <em>really</em> <em>really</em> insane question. I am helping a friend convert a <strong>single</strong> json file to csv thats <strong>180</strong> <em>terabytes</em>. The structure is basically <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">Map&lt;String, List&lt;I64&gt;&gt;</code>,and i need all the <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">List&lt;I64&gt;</code> in a csv file. (each new line in csv file = different entry in map).

This insanity was born from some dev who somehow didn&#39;t realize that JSON is a terrible format for this, they have now completed their course and left. (its uh, a college project)


I wrote some code, but let&#39;s be real. I am human, and I cannot make something that absurdly fast in a single day. My current code will take 13-14 days to completely convert this. (its purely single threaded because the real bottleneck is IO)


Is there anyway (some tool perhaps) i could go faster? i would like to get it down to 24 hours ish. </span> <span class=chatlog__reply-edited-timestamp title="Thursday, December 19, 2024 7:36 PM">(edited)</span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=rebirch data-user-id=984386111709253672>reBirch</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Friday, December 20, 2024 9:51 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1319648345484034130>12/20/2024 9:51 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I was going to say that AWS offers ridiculously high RAM EC2s (for running stuff like SAP HANA at scale)... but then I checked, and the largest they offer, at eyewatering 400 bucks an hour (ignoring the transfer price which I&#39;m sure is not trivial at this scale)... is about 32 TB. You&#39;d need 6 of these beasts in some sort of cluster, and that&#39;s assuming you can do something about IO locking. (which is like, a basic sata ssd, so i assume it would be much faster in practice)

it doesn&#39;t parse anything, it just goes through the bytes, uses a buffered read/write, and just pastes to the output file. i am not even parsing numbers, its just 21 byte fixed array that&#39;s immediately written to the output buffer.

no fast and used-in-production json parser supports streaming of this kind, not even simdjson, so i am not sure &quot;how&quot; i can make it faster.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1319653085177446440 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1319653085177446440><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Friday, December 20, 2024 10:10 AM">10:10 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>any benchmark i do is practically useless due to how large 180 TB is</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1319653121496055919 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1319653121496055919><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Friday, December 20, 2024 10:10 AM">10:10 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>and i dunno of any other tool i could use except that python library</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Friday, December 20, 2024 10:10 AM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>

Specifically
<div class="chatlog__markdown-quote"><div class="chatlog__markdown-quote-border"></div><div class="chatlog__markdown-quote-content">One example is chained time window aggregations, where users want to define another time window against the time window. </div></div><code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--multiline language-python">words = ...  # streaming DataFrame of schema { timestamp: Timestamp, word: String }

# Group the data by window and word and compute the count of each group

    window(words.timestamp, &quot;10 minutes&quot;, &quot;5 minutes&quot;),
    words.word
).count()

# Group the windowed data by another window and word and compute the count of each group
anotherWindowedCounts = windowedCounts.groupBy(
    window(windowedCounts.window, &quot;1 hour&quot;),
    windowedCounts.word
).count()</code></span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1321318143888588820 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1321318143888588820><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Wednesday, December 25, 2024 12:26 AM">12:26 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Would this end up being the count of say

Maybe I am too inexperienced to fully appreciate it, but I feel like this is a wonderful reference resource, but a pretty bad book.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1324151917340786719 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1324151917340786719><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Wednesday, January 1, 2025 8:06 PM">8:06 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Maybe it would have been better off as a wiki with paid access or something, or an encyclopedia. 
The sort of narrative path that Kleppmann takes is really not intuitive for me in some places, as well as some of the tangents that he goes on - they are good info, sure, but going through the book in the order in which it is written means that you have to go on the same tangents with him.
I also think what made it hard for me to get into was the decision to start with the really low-level things like B-trees, LSM-trees, and things like that, and then build up to distributed systems and ETL pipes. I think a book that started with very high-level abstractions and then got progressively lower down to the metal and reevaluated the assumptions about these abstractions would have been easier for me.</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Wednesday, January 1, 2025 8:18 PM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1327016873996587131 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1327016873996587131><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/689583717064114274/d5e507d4a2ed8b2d968e140cc0f1ba1a.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=wh00h00 data-user-id=689583717064114274>Wh00h00</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Thursday, January 9, 2025 5:51 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1327016873996587131>1/9/2025 5:51 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>why not just use vscode with the jupyter plugin ? am I missing something here? it can easily and nicely display stuff</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1327017889206898770 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1327017889206898770><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Thursday, January 9, 2025 5:55 PM">5:55 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>question.. I am doing some studying and for the purposes of fact modelling, I am seeing advice to not bring in anything that can be calculated. 
consider raw data that has something like 
<code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--multiline nohighlight">- shots_on_net
- total_goals
- shot_to_goal_conversion_pct</code>
apparently it is best to just grab the first 2 and calculate out the 3rd one instead of grabbing the <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">pct</code> from the source. Is it the idea that <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">pct</code> can be wrong, and thus calculating it yourself is better ? that calls into question the input and why <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">pct</code> might be wrong.. shouldn&#39;t this be dealt with upstream instead of basically re-making the source ?</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1327048302562119731 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1327048302562119731><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/105378403699408896/6ad9a21f4adaeee654f83a08a1327a68.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/689583717064114274/d5e507d4a2ed8b2d968e140cc0f1ba1a.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=wh00h00>Wh00h00</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1327017889206898770')"> question.. I am doing some studying and for the purposes of fact modelling, I am seeing advice to not bring in anything that can be calculated. 
consider raw data that has something like 
<code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--multiline nohighlight">- shots_on_net
- total_goals
- shot_to_goal_conversion_pct</code>
apparently it is best to just grab the first 2 and calculate out the 3rd one instead of grabbing the <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">pct</code> from the source. Is it the idea that <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">pct</code> can be wrong, and thus calculating it yourself is better ? that calls into question the input and why <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">pct</code> might be wrong.. shouldn&#39;t this be dealt with upstream instead of basically re-making the source ? </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author style=color:rgb(231,76,60) title=emikachi data-user-id=105378403699408896>emily</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Thursday, January 9, 2025 7:56 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1327048302562119731>1/9/2025 7:56 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>in this case specifically, if i&#39;m understanding your data right, <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">shot_to_goal_conversion_pct</code> stored on that fact is a <em>non-additive measure</em>. you can&#39;t meaningfully do any analytics on that number (sum, avg, etc.) across any dimension, it only makes sense record-wise at the same grain that the fact is already in (one row per team per game?)</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Thursday, January 9, 2025 8:06 PM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1327049266618961981 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1327049266618961981><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Thursday, January 9, 2025 8:00 PM">8:00 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>assuming you also had dimensions on the fact like <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">team_id</code> and <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">season_id</code>, you can make a more meaningful measure by calculating it as <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">sum(total_goals)/sum(shots_on_net)</code> <em>after</em> aggregating by team (useful), season (less useful but has meaning), or season <em>and</em> team</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Thursday, January 9, 2025 8:03 PM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1327050540970151989 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1327050540970151989><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Thursday, January 9, 2025 8:05 PM">8:05 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>hopefully that&#39;s a good enough explanation, but for more info you can search <em>non-additive fact measures</em></span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1327056589420625991 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1327056589420625991><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/689583717064114274/d5e507d4a2ed8b2d968e140cc0f1ba1a.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=wh00h00 data-user-id=689583717064114274>Wh00h00</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Thursday, January 9, 2025 8:29 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1327056589420625991>1/9/2025 8:29 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>that makes perfect sense thanks for that explanation.. so based on that then,  it is fair to say that for data testing, you may not need to carry it with you, but it is an easy way to check for consistency in downstream objects. you can simply use shots/ total and see if it matches to the pct, and know right away that the math is fine or not.</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1327057527820517449 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1327057527820517449><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/1296242089209626657/abea10f90dc6835f237e05650755d213.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author style=color:rgb(52,152,219) title=datacole data-user-id=1296242089209626657>Cole</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Thursday, January 9, 2025 8:32 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1327057527820517449>1/9/2025 8:32 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>So the question you ask yourself is: &quot;Why should I store this instead of re-calculating it each time I need it?&quot; Storage has a cost - it takes up extra space and makes your schema more complex.

And when you store a measure that can be calculated from your other columns, you&#39;re going to want some combination of:
<ul><li>You need to use it often (e.g. it simplifies a solid chunk of your expected query workload)</li><li>It&#39;s additive or at least semi-additive</li><li>It&#39;s expensive/slow to calculate</li></ul></span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1327058028058644611 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1327058028058644611><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Thursday, January 9, 2025 8:34 PM">8:34 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>And math is math and should be consistent. If your sum(shots) / sum(goals) is not equal to your conversion% in any scenario or in any setting, that implies you have an upstream data issue.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

Also about not being a programming whizz and being able to code. First, unless you will be building your own distributed computation framework or something, DE is not SWE, the tolerance for less polished code that does not leverage all the features of your language is higher - architecting skills and knowledge of specific tooling (specific databases, processing frameworks, orchestrators, etc) you are working with matter more here.
Also x2, it&#39;s great that you google when you code! It&#39;d be much worse if you didn&#39;t and ran to someone more experienced for advice on every small thing instead. (To be clear, I think it&#39;s absolutely fine to ask for advice if you&#39;ve looked and can&#39;t find the answer or if the question is specific to your org, but if you&#39;re trying to exit vim or concatenate a string, google it.)</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Monday, January 13, 2025 8:57 PM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1328609026564554792 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1328609026564554792><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/161154369763409921/d760257b5ffd16af7a8fa7056574cc51.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author style=color:rgb(46,204,113) title=kahnwong data-user-id=161154369763409921>kahnwong</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Tuesday, January 14, 2025 3:17 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1328609026564554792>1/14/2025 3:17 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Depends on what you are using it for. <div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1328662650850119723 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1328662650850119723><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/872204224904175636/93c5e37301273f5a0367371d9bd916f2.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=data_data_data data-user-id=872204224904175636>Aaron</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Tuesday, January 14, 2025 6:51 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1328662650850119723>1/14/2025 6:51 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Depends on the data. Sometimes it makes sense to fill missing cells with something like “n/a” or “unknown”, or even remove entire fields or rows if enough data is missing. Sometimes makes sense to find the average of the field (if numeric) and populate missing cells with the average. Sometimes issue can be fixed at the source. Really just depends on data and the downstream requirements</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Tuesday, January 14, 2025 7:19 AM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>

Also about not being a programming whizz and being able to code. First, unless you will be building your own distributed computation framework or something, DE is not SWE, the tolerance for less polished code that does not leverage all the features of your language is higher - architecting skills and knowledge of specific tooling (specific databases, processing frameworks, orchestrators, etc) you are working with matter more here.
Also x2, it&#39;s great that you google when you code! It&#39;d be much worse if you didn&#39;t and ran to someone more experienced for advice on every small thing instead. (To be clear, I think it&#39;s absolutely fine to ask for advice if you&#39;ve looked and can&#39;t find the answer or if the question is specific to your org, but if you&#39;re trying to exit vim or concatenate a string, google it.) </span> <span class=chatlog__reply-edited-timestamp title="Monday, January 13, 2025 8:57 PM">(edited)</span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=data_data_data data-user-id=872204224904175636>Aaron</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Tuesday, January 14, 2025 7:45 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1328676309777252432>1/14/2025 7:45 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Thanks! It&#39;s uncommon for something to scale better than linearly on performance, and that usually means that your lower-scale option is hitting a slowdown of some kind that the larger-scale option does not, which is going to happen when you&#39;re pushing the limits of your hardware in some way. This makes sense if you were scaling down until you started OOMing.

The main candidates I can think of are spilling to disk or a larger cache that&#39;s being used more effectively without as many invalidations or reconstructions of artifacts.</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Tuesday, January 21, 2025 9:32 PM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1331420647590592563 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1331420647590592563><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Tuesday, January 21, 2025 9:30 PM">9:30 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>But yeah, better-than-linear performance scaling is possible, and because cost is (basically) always linear, this isn&#39;t too good to be true - but it&#39;s very neat.</span></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=thumbsup><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=👍 src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f44d.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>1</span></div></div></div></div></div></div>

<ul><li>is the data always gonna be in a similar format?</li><li>how often and how much data are you ingesting ?</li><li>what business questions and temporal resolution are you looking to answer them on ? are they more BI-based or AI/ ML based?</li><li>how much infra do you have ?</li><li>are you worried about vendor lockin (basically if you are on databricks, delta lake is more optimized and integrated with the catalog)</li><li>are you going to need to do a ton of time travelling / partition re-arranging ?</li><li>how mature is the data org / is this greenfield or is there already something set up</li></ul></span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Wednesday, January 22, 2025 7:13 PM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1331791962231144539 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1331791962231144539><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/689583717064114274/d5e507d4a2ed8b2d968e140cc0f1ba1a.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/0.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=ccccccc1010>Gary</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1331749876064718940')"> I actually wanted to ask what is the real life use case of time travel?
Will you treat this features as s features that you rely on in terms on version control instead of making use of schema design like SCD type2 or other techniques? </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=wh00h00 data-user-id=689583717064114274>Wh00h00</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, January 22, 2025 10:05 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1331791962231144539>1/22/2025 10:05 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>off the top of my head, SCD2 only really works when the temporal resolution matches. if you create source / staging iceberg tables, and if your pipeline is down for a few days, you can backfill SCD2 each day with timetravel rather than a single day.. that way you don&#39;t lose resolution.. also.. SCD2 can theoretically fail, with timetravel, you always have the table as it was at that time.</span></div></div></div></div></div>
